There\\n11: /// is no \\\"pass\\\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\\n18: /// single module provided.\\n19: ///\\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\\n21: /// modules and functions.\\n22: ///\\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\\n24: ///   a Function.\\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\\n26: ///\\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \\\"Value Semantics and Concept-based\\n29: /// Polymorphism\\\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \\\"Inheritance Is The Base\\n30: /// Class of Evil\\\") by Sean Parent:\\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\\n33: /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\\n34: ///\\n35: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n36: \\n37: #ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\\n38: #define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\\n39: \\n40: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\\\"\\n41: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\\\"\\n42: #include \\\"llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h\\\"\\n47: #include \\\"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\\\"\\n48: #include \\\"llvm/Support/TypeName.h\\\"\\n49: #include <cassert>\\n50: #include <cstring>\\n51: #include <list>\\n52: #include <memory>\\n53: #include <tuple>\\n54: #include <type_traits>\\n55: #include <utility>\\n56: #include <vector>\\n57: \\n58: namespace llvm {\\n59: \\n60: class Function;\\n61: class Module;\\n62: \\n63: // Forward declare the analysis manager template.\\n64: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\\n65: \\n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\\n67: /// passes.\\n68: ///\\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\\n72:   static StringRef name() {\\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n74:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\\n76:     Name.consume_front(\\\"llvm::\\\");\\n77:     return Name;\\n78:   }\\n79: \\n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\\n84:     OS << PassName;\\n85:   }\\n86: };\\n87: \\n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\\n89: ///\\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\n95:   ///\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\n99:   ///\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\c AnalysisKey\\n101:   /// member called \\\\c Key.\\n102:   ///\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\\n164: public:\\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\\n167: \\n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\\n171:   // duplicated code here.\\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\\n173: \\n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\\n176:     return *this;\\n177:   }\\n178: \\n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\\\",\\\");\\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\\n183:       OS << LS;\\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\\n185:     }\\n186:   }\\n187: \\n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\\n202:   }\\n203: \\n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\\n209:   template <typename PassT>\\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\\n214:   }\\n215: \\n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\\n218: \\n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\\n220: \\n221: protected:\\n222:   using PassConceptT =\\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n224: \\n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\\n226: };\\n227: \\n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\\n230: \\n231: template <>\\n232: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n233:                                                    const Module &IR);\\n234: \\n235: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Module>;\\n236: \\n237: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over modules.\\n238: using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;\\n239: \\n240: template <>\\n241: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n242:                                                      const Function &IR);\\n243: \\n244: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Function>;\\n245: \\n246: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over functions.\\n247: using FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>;\\n248: \\n249: /// A container for analyses that lazily runs them and caches their\\n250: /// results.\\n251: ///\\n252: /// This class can manage analyses for any IR unit where the address of the IR\\n253: /// unit sufficies as its identity.\\n254: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... None of these APIs should be used elsewhere.\n14: ///\n15: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n16: \n17: #ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGERINTERNAL_H\n18: #define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGERINTERNAL_H\n19: \n20: #include \"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\"\n21: #include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n22: #include \"llvm/IR/Analysis.h\"\n23: #include \"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\"\n24: #include <memory>\n25: #include <type_traits>\n26: #include <utility>\n27: \n28: namespace llvm {\n29: \n30: template <typename IRUnitT> class AllAnalysesOn;\n31: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs>\n40: struct PassConcept {\n41:   // Boiler plate necessary for the container of derived classes.\n42:   virtual ~PassConcept() = default;\n43: \n44:   /// The polymorphic API which runs the pass over a given IR entity.\n45:   ///\n46:   /// Note that actual pass object can omit the analysis manager argument if\n47:   /// desired. Also that the analysis manager may be null if there is no\n48:   /// analysis manager in the pass pipeline.\n49:   virtual PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\n50:                                 ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs) = 0;\n51: \n52:   virtual void\n53:   printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\n54:                 function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) = 0;\n55:   /// Polymorphic method to access the name of a pass.\n56:   virtual StringRef name() const = 0;\n57: \n58:   /// Polymorphic method to let a pass optionally exempted from skipping by\n59:   /// PassInstrumentation.\n60:   /// To opt-in, pass should implement `static bool isRequired()`. It's no-op\n61:   /// to have `isRequired` always return false since that is the default.\n62:   virtual bool isRequired() const = 0;\n63: };\n64: \n65: /// A template wrapper used to implement the polymorphic API.\n66: ///\n67: /// Can be instantiated for any object which provides a \\c run method accepting\n68: /// an \\c IRUnitT& and an \\c AnalysisManager<IRUnit>&. It requires the pass to\n69: /// be a copyable object.\n70: template <typename IRUnitT, typename PassT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\n71:           typename... ExtraArgs) override {\n91:     return Pass.run(IR, AM, ExtraArgs...);\n92:   }\n93: \n94:   void printPipeline(\n95:       raw_ostream &OS,\n96:       function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) override {\n97:     Pass.printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\n98:   }\n99: \n100:   StringRef name() const override { return PassT::name(); }\n101: \n102:   template <typename T>\n103:   using has_required_t = decltype(std::declval<T &>().isRequired());\n104: \n105:   template <typename T> static bool passIsRequiredImpl() {\n106:     if constexpr (is_detected<has_required_t, T>::value)\n107:       return T::isRequired();\n108:     return false;\n109:   }\n110: \n111:   bool isRequired() const override { return passIsRequiredImpl<PassT>(); }\n112: \n113:   PassT Pass;\n114: };\n115: \n116: /// Abstract concept of an analysis result.\n117: ///\n118: /// This concept is parameterized over the IR unit that this result pertains\n119: /// to.\n120: template <typename IRUnitT, typename InvalidatorT>\n121: struct AnalysisResultConcept {\n122:   virtual ~AnalysisResultConcept() = default;\n123: \n124:   /// Method to try and mark a result as invalid.\n125:   ///\n126:   /// When the outer analysis manager detects a change in some underlying\n127:   /// unit of the IR, it will call this method on all of the results cached.\n128:   ///\n129:   /// \\p PA is a set of preserved analyses which can be used to avoid\n130:   /// invalidation because the pass which changed the underlying IR took care\n131:   /// to update or preserve the analysis result in some way.\n132:   ///\n133:   /// \\p Inv is typically a \\c AnalysisManager::Invalidator object that can be\n134:   /// used by a particular analysis result to discover if other analyses\n135:   /// results are also invalidated in the event that this result depends on\n136:   /// them. template-based architecture defined in llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h. The PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...> template (lines 159-226) implements a generic pass manager that can manage passes over any IR unit (Module, Function, Loop, etc.). This template provides:\\n\\n1. **addPass() method** (lines 193-214): Accepts a pass instance and wraps it in a PassModel concept wrapper, storing it in a std::vector for sequential execution\\n2. **run() method** (lines 190-191): Executes all contained passes sequentially over the IR unit, propagating the AnalysisManager to each pass for dependency resolution\\n3. **PreservedAnalyses tracking**: Each pass reports which analyses it preserves, enabling the AnalysisManager to invalidate stale results\\n\\nThe ModulePassManager typedef (line 238) is a convenience specialization for Module-level passes: `using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;`\\n\\n## PassRegistry Registration System\\n\\nPass registration follows a two-tier system defined in llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h and implemented in llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp:\\n\\n1. **PassInfo metadata** (llvm/include/llvm/PassInfo.h, lines 29-89): Each pass has a PassInfo instance containing:\\n   - PassName: Display name of the pass\\n   - PassArgument: Command-line argument to invoke the pass\\n   - PassID: Type-erased identifier (&MyPass::ID)\\n   - NormalCtor: Default constructor function pointer\\n\\n2. **PassRegistry::registerPass()** (llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp, lines 48-62): Global singleton registry that maintains two maps:\\n   - PassInfoMap: Maps PassID (void*) to PassInfo pointer\\n   - PassInfoStringMap: Maps PassArgument (StringRef) to PassInfo pointer\\n   - Listeners: PassRegistrationListener callbacks for observers\\n\\n3. **Registration macros** (llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h, lines 39-58):\\n   - INITIALIZE_PASS_BEGIN/END: Defines a pass initialization function that creates PassInfo and registers it\\n   - RegisterPass<T> template (lines 89-98): Simple registration helper that calls PassRegistry::registerPass()\\n\\n## Pass Concept and Polymorphism\\n\\nThe pass system uses concept-based polymorphism (not inheritance) defined in llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h:\\n\\n1. **PassConcept** (lines 40-63): Abstract interface for pass objects with virtual methods:\\n   - run(IRUnitT&, AnalysisManagerT&, ExtraArgTs...): Executes the pass\\n   - printPipeline(): Prints pass name for debugging\\n   - isRequired(): Indicates if pass should skip instrumentation\\n\\n2. **PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>** (lines 72-114): Type-erased wrapper that adapts any pass object conforming to the run() protocol into the PassConcept interface. This enables storing heterogeneous pass types in a single vector.\\n\\n## Pipeline Construction: PassBuilder\\n\\nThe PassBuilder class (llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h) orchestrates standard optimization pipelines:\\n\\n1. **buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline()** (llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp, lines 1715-1761):\\n   -
